  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_516632e4-58f7-4029-a6fb-c2d96ddf00b7'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I received this book for my 12th birthday in April of 1985. The book had just came out and my mom got it from Waldenbooks . I still have all my dragon<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I received this book for my 12th birthday in April of 1985. The book had just came out and my mom got it from Waldenbooks . I still have all my dragonlance collection and still looks brand new . So yeah enjoy the book. I have fond memories of the series. If you want, here is a site to read the books in chronological order. But the Chronicles series is what most of us started out with - <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.alltimelines.com/dragonlance/">https://www.alltimelines.com/dragonla...</a><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_906612678" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/906612678" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/906612678?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10103077-dragons-of-winter-night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=dungeons-and-dragons">dungeons-and-dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2015">2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=dragonlance">dragonlance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer906612678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17932348691933401955">This is not the rating this book deserves, but I suppose it is the one it needs right now.<br/><br/>All evidence suggests that the old gods are finally returning to Krynn after centuries of exile. The Dragon Highlords and their armies of darkness are marching all over the world, conquering everything in their way. Meanwhile, our band of heroes is split apart in a search for the lost dragon orbs, which may be the key to turning the tide in the war…<br/><br/>Imagine reading a version of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> where El</span>
  <span id="freeText17932348691933401955" style="display:none">This is not the rating this book deserves, but I suppose it is the one it needs right now.<br /><br />All evidence suggests that the old gods are finally returning to Krynn after centuries of exile. The Dragon Highlords and their armies of darkness are marching all over the world, conquering everything in their way. Meanwhile, our band of heroes is split apart in a search for the lost dragon orbs, which may be the key to turning the tide in the war…<br /><br />Imagine reading a version of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> where Elrond turns away the hobbits because they’re inferior to the proud elves; where the Council of Rivendell is on the verge of becoming a massacre when every single nation and people claims possession of the One Ring; where Gondor and Rohan go to full-scale war over a petty grievance while the armies of Mordor invade from the east; where the Fellowship is broken apart by constant quarrelling between everyone and everything. Then you can probably understand how frustrating this book was to read.<br /><br />This second volume of the Dragonlance Chronicles was in many ways a disaster. Almost the entirety of the book was one-star material. There was a huge amount of repetition (with this book repeating both the first book and itself), most of the characters were frustrating on a throw-book-in-wall level (including fan favourites and some of my own favourite characters), and last but not least it was really, really, really, really boring.<br /><br />And all that leads to even more problems. Even the first book had plenty of weak points. But because of the fascinating parts of that one, I was perfectly willing to ignore them. Unfortunately, those parts are all gone in this book, which in turn makes it virtually impossible to overlook the flaws. Dragonlance is at best mindless entertainment, and when the entertainment is gone, it is, logically, just mindless.<br /><br />Luckily the book did improve in the end. Weis &amp; Hickman managed to introduce a great character and re-introduce an <i>amazing</i> character. And there is actually a character dying! So far, “death” in this series has been a minor setback where a character is removed from the plot for a short period of time only to return heroically later on. So this was actually a welcome addition to the plot, even though I rather liked said character. These reasons are what made me give the book two stars instead of one, and they also made me quite a bit more hopeful for reading the last book in the trilogy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17932348691933401955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1484921354" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484921354" />
    <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries"><img alt="Mayim de Vries" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1560508357p2/50424456.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1484921354?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mayim de Vries" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mayim de Vries" href="/user/show/50424456-mayim-de-vries">Mayim de Vries</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1484921354" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12800002225878689062"><b>“I saw two roads stretching before us. If we take the easiest, it will appear the best at the beginning, but darkness will fall at the end, never to be lifted. If we take the other road, it will be hard and difficult to travel. It could cost the lives of some we love. Worse, it might cots others their very souls. But only through these great sacrifices will we find hope.”</b><br/><br/>The Queen of Darkness and the Warrior constellations are missing from the sky because the gods returned to Krynn and are locke</span>
  <span id="freeText12800002225878689062" style="display:none"><b>“I saw two roads stretching before us. If we take the easiest, it will appear the best at the beginning, but darkness will fall at the end, never to be lifted. If we take the other road, it will be hard and difficult to travel. It could cost the lives of some we love. Worse, it might cots others their very souls. But only through these great sacrifices will we find hope.”</b><br /><br />The Queen of Darkness and the Warrior constellations are missing from the sky because the gods returned to Krynn and are locked in the ultimate fight of good against the evil. Our protagonists won a battle but they are a long way from winning the war, and it seems that their odds turn from bad to worse. <b>Please note that my rating disclaimer* still holds</b> for the second volume of the Dragonlance Chronicles.<br /><br />The <b>forces of darkness command armies of draconian and the hosts of dragons, the forces of good are essentially reduced to a band of companions</b> including <b>half-elf Tanis</b>; <b>Flint the dwarf</b>; <b>Sturm, a paladin</b> aspiring to the knighthood in the ancient order of Solamnia; twin <b>brothers Caramon and Raistlin</b> combining the strength of muscle of the former and the power of magic in the frail body of the latter; <b>Tika a feisty ex-tavern girl</b>; an <b>elflord Gilthanas and his sister Laurana</b> (badly infatuated with Tanis); <b>Elistan, a cleric of Paladine, and a cleric of Mishakal Goldmoon</b> with her husband <b>Riverwind</b>, and, last but not least, <b>Tasslehoff Burrfoot of the kenderfolk</b>. <br /><br />The main argument against the Dragonlance Chronicles, frequently repeated in several reviews, implies that since the whole plot was conceived during a RPG session, it renders the whole thing worthless or, in the best case, it places the series on the level of bad fan-fiction. I’d like to remind you that the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577764482?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Malazan Book of the Fallen</a>, which many believe to be the best contemporary epic fantasy, also resulted from hours of game-play between friends. Thus, it is not the about where the ideas of the book comes from, but rather about the idea and how it is executed. The truth is that <b>the Dragonlance Chronicles are badly written</b>. The main characteristic feature of this prose is the <b>absolute abuse of adjectives and adverbs</b> that does not leave a shroud of doubt whether given character is good or evil. All the good ones are gentle, have strong albeit delicate arms, soft and sweet voices, grieved faces, are lithe and delicate with quiet gallantry whereas all the bad ones laugh in an unpleasant way, have sinister looks, rasping voices and so on and so forth. I will be the first to admit, that compared with Malazan the Dragonlance is like a child’s drawing juxtaposed with the frescoes in the Sistine Chapel. Still, it has it charms.<br /><br />Arguably, the first book was very character driven and told us how the adventuring party was formed. <b>What do you do once you compose your adventuring party? You break it up, of course</b> (even Professor Tolkien knew that). The companions separate pursuing the new quests; they need to <b>find the dragon orbs</b> – three of those artifacts survived the Cataclysm and need to be recovered if the dragon armies are to be defeated. There is also the mystery of the fabled dragonlance to be uncovered.<br /><br />While the <b>tale is more plot-centred</b> this time (<b>clumsily, as huge chunks of the story are omitted and readers will be lost</b>, particularly at the beginning of the book, and then again when starting part II), there is still <b>character development, especially when it comes to Sturm and Laurana</b>. We finally get to <b>meet Kitiara</b> (overall, the <b>romance subplots are much more pronounced</b> in this instalment), have the chance to visit <b>fascinating new locations</b> – the elven city of Silvanesti, a city of Tarsis the Beautiful, the gnome mountain of Nevermind, and an ancient tower of Palanthas. <b>You will also, undoubtedly, be thrilled to read about <i>“the first, last, and only time”</i> when Tas was struck speechless</b> and sad to <b>say goodbye to some</b> for whom fighting for things bigger than your life is worth more than life itself. <br /><br /><b>The Dragons of Winter Nights is my ultimate guilty pleasure</b>: a gripping adventure, not too profound, some melodrama mixed with silly humour and a heart-warming message. You can always ask for more but sometimes this is enough. <br /><br /><br /><b>*Disclaimer: My rating is purely sentimental. Dragons of Winter Night is a read down the memory lane. If I were to rate it on the basis of my current standards and preferences, it would score 3 stars the most.</b><br /><br />Also in the series: <br /><br />1. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484918749?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Autumn Twilight</a><br />3. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484921581" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Spring Dawning</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12800002225878689062" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText9644523649579705671" style="display:none">i read this in secret, because i was embarrassed, but now i am embarrassed that i was embarrassed and basically it's a vicious and hideous neverending cycle of guilt and shame. there are far more important books i could and should be reading. there are works of Great Literature on my shelf, glaring at me balefully while i devour these dragon books like a geeky ten year old boy. whatever, man. anyone who doesn't see the appeal of dragons and adventure and elves and dragons and shit just has no soul. or something.<br /><br />this one was far better written than the last, though there were still points where i giggled uncontrollably because of the rampant corny cliches. the characters are far better drawn as well, and i am ashamed to say that i actually shed a tear when sturm died. he was a good guy, and so much more fully bad-ass than the whining hero of the story, it's ridiculous. i also stick by my initial evaluation of really liking the kender, who reminds me of me at my annoying best, and the wizard fizban. i, um, am reading the next one mainly to find out what happens to them. the very ambiguous wizard kid is also pretty intriguing, actually. anyway! the third one will be the last one for me. until i move in with chris, because he has like a whole bunch more of them or something. it's like, um, you know, candy is good for your soul!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_18713436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/18713436" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/18713436?book_show_action=true">Mar 26, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=to-my-kids">to-my-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer18713436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5515463435118112834">I have read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23454.Dragons_of_Winter_Night__Dragonlance_Chronicles___2_' title='Dragons of Winter Night (Dragonlance Chronicles, #2) by Margaret Weis' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragons of Winter Night</a> a number of times since it was first published, and it has always been my favourite of the Chronicles.<br/><br/>This time I just finished reading it out loud to my four year olds. A long undertaking, and one that was necessarily sporadic. Some nights we read, others we didn't, and how much we read was dependent on levels of sleepiness, focus and interest. But it was well worth the effort because my kids loved the story, and I can see it helping to expand their imaginati</span>
  <span id="freeText5515463435118112834" style="display:none">I have read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23454.Dragons_of_Winter_Night__Dragonlance_Chronicles___2_" title="Dragons of Winter Night (Dragonlance Chronicles, #2) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Winter Night</a> a number of times since it was first published, and it has always been my favourite of the Chronicles.<br /><br />This time I just finished reading it out loud to my four year olds. A long undertaking, and one that was necessarily sporadic. Some nights we read, others we didn't, and how much we read was dependent on levels of sleepiness, focus and interest. But it was well worth the effort because my kids loved the story, and I can see it helping to expand their imaginations. <br /><br />This time through I also nailed down the main reason I love the Chronicles, and why it is still one of the best fantasy series ever inspired by Dungeons and Dragons -- the way in which it undercuts fantasy's usual racial hierarchies.<br /><br />One of the major problems I have long had with fantasy is the inherent racism that fantasy perpetuates. Fantasy generally entrenches the concept of "good" and "evil" races (which even Dragonlance can't entirely escape), and this, in turn, leads to a hierarchy of races with the Elves as the "superior race" and some of the monstrous humanoid races as the "inferior races."<br /><br />This scares me. It scares me because when I bring this flaw up in discussion of Tolkien or Lewis or other "great" fantasy writers, people fight me passionately and refuse to recognize that a problem even exists. It frightens me that most people who recognize the issue don't see anything wrong with racial hierarchies in fantasy (usually tossing out the old confection "it's only a story" as an argument). It scares me because all of this also entrenches a frighteningly simplistic vision of good and evil. A black and white world view that simply doesn't exist and makes us capable of evil because we are sure of our own goodness. <br /><br />But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/259836.Dragons_of_Autumn_Twilight__Dragonlance_Chronicles___1_" title="Dragons of Autumn Twilight (Dragonlance Chronicles, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonlance</a> makes race an issue, and no race is immune to evil deeds. We have bad knights, bad Qualinesti elves, bad Silvanesti elves, bad and good dragons, heroic but racist dwarves, a bastard half-elf that no one can accept, tribal barbarians fighting through their prejudices towards the civilized world, a lover and friend of the heroes in charge of the Dragonarmies, and a pseudo-evil wizard who saves them all. <br /><br />There is very little black and white in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/259836.Dragons_of_Autumn_Twilight__Dragonlance_Chronicles___1_" title="Dragons of Autumn Twilight (Dragonlance Chronicles, #1) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonlance</a>, although it still appears in the forms of Paladine (Fizban) and Takhisis, and unlike other fantasy series -- even the great ones but particularly others in the D&amp;D ouevre (see the Drizzt Do'Urden series) -- it is filled with far more shades of gray.<br /><br />It may seem like a pulpy little distraction, but the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23454.Dragons_of_Winter_Night__Dragonlance_Chronicles___2_" title="Dragons of Winter Night (Dragonlance Chronicles, #2) by Margaret Weis" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragons of Winter Night</a>, and the entire Chronicles, is more than that. It is series that can help to shape a new vision of ethics in fantasy literature. And I hope that's something my kids take away from the experience. I will do my best to make sure they do.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5515463435118112834" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Both series are remarkable on their own right, however, both dissatisfied me in the end: both stories lack verosimility, and Martin`s characters showed inconsistencies quite hard to buy (though in Dying Of The Light, for example, the story and the characters were flawless - but that was science fiction, and we are speaking now of fantasy).<br/>I loved far better Stackpole`s Age Of Disco</span>
  <span id="freeText5878249924410884542" style="display:none">I have read both Tolkien`s Lord of the Rings and Martin`s A Song Of Ice And Fire - to a certain degree of pleasure. Both series are remarkable on their own right, however, both dissatisfied me in the end: both stories lack verosimility, and Martin`s characters showed inconsistencies quite hard to buy (though in Dying Of The Light, for example, the story and the characters were flawless - but that was science fiction, and we are speaking now of fantasy).<br />I loved far better Stackpole`s Age Of Discovery and Abercrombie`s First Law, but Dragons Of Winter Night stands, undoubtedly, as the best fantasy book, with the most fascinating characters, of the subgenre, and I can hardly imagine how could someone beat such a complex and wonderful story, and such an elegant writing style.<br />This book is the very definition of dark/high/epic fantasy - at its best.</span>

  <span id="freeText3210878821150501124" style="display:none">Okay. Yes, I still love these books. But at the same time I am not blind to their faults. It's like loving your husband of twenty years even though he now has a beer belly, has lost most of his hair, leaves the toilet seat up and chews with his mouth open. <br /><br />Every stereotype of fantasy is here. <div id="review_350753238" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/350753238" />
    <a title="Jim C" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c"><img alt="Jim C" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340034171p2/10296231.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/350753238?book_show_action=true">Jun 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim C" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim C" href="/user/show/10296231-jim-c">Jim C</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer350753238" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13830885793951557137">This is the second book of a trilogy and the first book must be read before this one. In this one, we have a little bit of a time jump. The conclusion of the first book was the rescue of the humans by our companions. This one starts off with those humans residing with the dwarves and everything is not okay. Good might have won the battle against evil but the war is far from over.<br/><br/>I have read this trilogy several times and this easily gets a five star rating from me just for the nostalgic factor. </span>
  <span id="freeText13830885793951557137" style="display:none">This is the second book of a trilogy and the first book must be read before this one. In this one, we have a little bit of a time jump. The conclusion of the first book was the rescue of the humans by our companions. This one starts off with those humans residing with the dwarves and everything is not okay. Good might have won the battle against evil but the war is far from over.<br /><br />I have read this trilogy several times and this easily gets a five star rating from me just for the nostalgic factor. I will admit that this book does suffer a little from middle book syndrome but it more than makes up for it with its emotional impact. Seriously, every time I read that finale I get choked up. It might be the best scene in the whole trilogy and it is the one scene I would love to see if these books were ever made into movies. The one problem this book has is that our main companions take a back seat to others. Don't get me wrong. The stories of others are terrific reads especially the character growth of Laurana. It is a departure from the first book as Tanis, Raistlin, and Tas really don't have much character development in this book. But this book does delve into other aspects like racism, love, and politics and it all works.<br /><br />I am probably being a little generous with my rating. This is still an excellent read after all these years but it might be the weakest book of the trilogy. That being said it put many smiles on my face with the adventures and also kicked me in the stomach with the feels. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13830885793951557137" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780140087192" href="/book/show/1081831.Dragons_of_Winter_Night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15413983-helen?shelf=silly-in-a-bad-way">silly-in-a-bad-way</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2155643256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9358309859522669353">Why is everyone so down on Raistlin? He consistently saves everyone every time they're in danger. They'd be dead (well, Dragonlance dead, which is dead until they're needed again for the story) 100 times over if it weren't for him. <br/><br/>The raging sexism is also starting to annoy me. It's a fantasy world, why do the elves have to stick to old-school European rules too? Why are all the women appraised on how beautiful they are? <br/><br/>And I really wish the authors hadn't tried to put romance in, it's instalo</span>
  <span id="freeText9358309859522669353" style="display:none">Why is everyone so down on Raistlin? He consistently saves everyone every time they're in danger. They'd be dead (well, Dragonlance dead, which is dead until they're needed again for the story) 100 times over if it weren't for him. <br /><br />The raging sexism is also starting to annoy me. It's a fantasy world, why do the elves have to stick to old-school European rules too? Why are all the women appraised on how beautiful they are? <br /><br />And I really wish the authors hadn't tried to put romance in, it's instalove so badly done it makes me angry. Laurana needs to leave Tanis in the dust.<br /><br />Last thing I want to moan about - the massive time skips where characters go off and have adventures and come back with wondrous objects are annoying. I think most of them are filled in with later books but it seems like a bit of a cheap way to keep us reading the Dragonlance series. If I hadn't already read the first in the Lost Chronicle series I would have been convinced I'd missed a whole book. I can't imagine how annoyed people who read them in the 20 years before the Lost Chronicle's were published must have felt. <br /><br />Other than that, these are fun, fluffy fantasy adventures. If you can ignore the fact that they're aimed at teenage boys and were written in the 80s they are good escapism, and I'm finding them a bit addictive.<br /><br />Like chocolate digestives in book form, these are comforting and fun but not necessarily good for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9358309859522669353" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8940288751266785907">Spoiler Haven. <br/>I wavered between a 4 and 5. I almost feel guilty not giving this the perfect score. It was still a fantastic book.<br/><br/>The Good<br/>Everyone stepped up to their destinies and their character shined.   <span id="freeText8940288751266785907" style="display:none">Spoiler Haven. <br />I wavered between a 4 and 5. I almost feel guilty not giving this the perfect score. It was still a fantastic book.<br /><br />The Good<br />Everyone stepped up to their destinies and their character shined. Gut wrenching drama interspersed with the right touches of humour to keep the reader from going mad with grief.<br /><br />The traveling magic show really sat well with me. It was a glimpse of what might have been in a happier time. If there is a William the pig story I will scream!<br /><br />The ending, though needed, was truly heartbreaking. Long live Sturm Brightblade.<br /><br />The Bad<br />Two forced pure and true love stories. I believed in Riverwind and Goldmoon. Riverwind went to the ends of the plains, fighting impossible odds for years to come out on top. I just didn't buy either here. It moved the story along but this is really what kept me from being wholly invested.<br /><br />The Ugly<br />Gilthanas found out the woman he was intimate with was a Dragon. In the reveal he was having a literal breakdown, crying and screaming, probably over the idea of Dragon headed babies and what goes where. You think Laurana could have comforted him, just a little? A tender hug, some kind words or an awkward pat on the back, maybe? </span>

<div id="review_1326227559" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1326227559" />
    <a title="Leona" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34997235-leona"><img alt="Leona" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1438676712p2/34997235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1326227559?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leona" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leona" href="/user/show/34997235-leona">Leona</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34997235-leona?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1326227559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15396315640059854621">I have been feeling quite ashamed for not getting around to reading the fantasy classics everyone read as teenagers, so I’m fixing it one book at a time. Dragons of Winter Night is more of a page turner compared to the first book, it’s thick with action, tension, suspense, twists and turns with a touch of humor. The scenes with Fizban and the gnomes were hilarious.<br/><br/>In this book things were surprisingly more grey than I expected. There’s no black and white and even the most honorable, utopic facti</span>
  <span id="freeText15396315640059854621" style="display:none">I have been feeling quite ashamed for not getting around to reading the fantasy classics everyone read as teenagers, so I’m fixing it one book at a time. Dragons of Winter Night is more of a page turner compared to the first book, it’s thick with action, tension, suspense, twists and turns with a touch of humor. The scenes with Fizban and the gnomes were hilarious.<br /><br />In this book things were surprisingly more grey than I expected. There’s no black and white and even the most honorable, utopic factions are marred with greed, infighting and political intrigue.<br /><br />The development of the characters is quite intriguing to read. We get to see the inner struggles of Tanis, Laurana, Sturm and even the Kender Tasslehoff. Raistlin’s power and magic skills keep increasing and his relationship with the companions somewhat improves (at least that was the impression I got.)<br /><br />We finally get to meet Tanis’ love interest Kitiara and I must say it came as a huge surprise and plot twist. For the sake of keeping this spoiler free, I can’t say more but I didn’t expect that at all, even though I read plenty of plot twists. Tanis is torn between the human woman Kitiara and the elf maiden, his childhood crush Laurana. I absolutely hate love triangles but the love triangle here was negligible enough so I was able to tolerate it.<br /><br />The Silvanesti scenes are bone chilling unless you are an experienced grimdark reader. I have to say the dark and creepy atmosphere was well done.<br /><br />Even though it has been 30 years since the publication of the Dragonlance Chronicles, the books still hold up today. This book is a page turner and a great read, I’m looking forward to reading the third book and then the Dragonlance Legends series after that. I really wish I’ve read those books as a teenager, but nevertheless they are still quite enjoyable, even at my age.<br /><br />Verdict: This is a must read for all fantasy readers, young and old alike.<br /><br /><br />My review is also posted here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://leonahenry.wordpress.com/2015/07/09/book-review-dragons-of-winter-night-by-margaret-weis-and-tracy-hickman/">https://leonahenry.wordpress.com/2015...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="15396315640059854621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_237855773" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/237855773" />
    <a title="Yoly" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6837622-yoly"><img alt="Yoly" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383074979p2/6837622.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/237855773?book_show_action=true">Nov 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yoly" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yoly" href="/user/show/6837622-yoly">Yoly</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/10103077-dragons-of-winter-night">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer237855773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12234333417014925308">The fourth time’s the charm?<br/><br/>So many things happen in this book, so many things that even though this is my fourth re-read I had forgotten. I don’t know if it’s nostalgia or that I needed to go back to Krynn or what, but this read felt amazing. I could hardly put it down, and I don’t remember feeling this way the previous times I read it. Maybe because I’m older (and hopefully wiser) I was able to appreciate everything that was going on. I also think this book has more depth than the previous one</span>
  <span id="freeText12234333417014925308" style="display:none">The fourth time’s the charm?<br /><br />So many things happen in this book, so many things that even though this is my fourth re-read I had forgotten. I don’t know if it’s nostalgia or that I needed to go back to Krynn or what, but this read felt amazing. I could hardly put it down, and I don’t remember feeling this way the previous times I read it. Maybe because I’m older (and hopefully wiser) I was able to appreciate everything that was going on. I also think this book has more depth than the previous one. If I remember correctly, TSR needed the first book to be self-contained, in case in didn’t sell, so the story felt a little “lite”. But after the success of the first book, they decided to do a trilogy, and it shows they had more room to develop the story and the characters.<br /><br />We finally get to see Kitiara on the page, my favorite character not only in Dragonlance, but in all of fantasy. I cheered every time she showed up (yes, I literally cheered. I’m that type of reader). I don’t know what it says about me that my favorite character is a villain, but I think the Dark Lady is awesome! :)<br /><br />In this book I also came to appreciate Tasslehoff a bit more. I found him kind of annoying on the previous book, but he has earned my respect in this one. Laurana is another character that I felt matured a lot in this book. I didn’t remember her being such a badass.<br /><br />2020 was the best read of this book for me.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12234333417014925308" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_328130022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/328130022" />
    <a title="Jenn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9453964-jenn"><img alt="Jenn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1437006922p2/9453964.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/328130022?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jenn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jenn" href="/user/show/9453964-jenn">Jenn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer328130022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9262178703731097603">The second book in the Dragonlance Trilogy series is a book that can not be put down! The story picks up with the companions after they have escaped Pax Tharkis and killed one of the Dragon Highlords. They fight their way across those country searching for answers to their questions, and find a way to win the war. The companions split up whilelooking for the mysterious dragon orbs and the long lost Dragonlances of children stories. Rasitlin continues to mysteriously get stronger as a strange voi</span>
  <span id="freeText9262178703731097603" style="display:none">The second book in the Dragonlance Trilogy series is a book that can not be put down! The story picks up with the companions after they have escaped Pax Tharkis and killed one of the Dragon Highlords. They fight their way across those country searching for answers to their questions, and find a way to win the war. The companions split up whilelooking for the mysterious dragon orbs and the long lost Dragonlances of children stories. Rasitlin continues to mysteriously get stronger as a strange voice whispers to him. Strum fights for his right to hold the title of being a knight, and Tanis struggles between his love for two women.<br /><br />As with Dragons of Autumn Twilight, Dragons of Winter Night has a great balance of humor, romance, mystery, action and suspense. While the book may be considered long, it is far from boring. You are thrown into the action from the beginning of the story, while the backstory is being told, just in case you forgot or didn't read Dragons of Autumn Twilight. One of the intriguing parts is the animosity between the races even the sub-races such as the Qualasti Elves, Silvanisti Elves and the Wilder Elves. It helps show one of the pitfallsto humanity and society. We get more of a background to the history of the world including the tower of High Socery and how the dragon orbs came into existance. The story progresses emmensly in this novel.<br /><br />The companions learn a lesson in friendship, trust and love amidst the battle between good and evil. The continue to search for the answer to the Disks as well as the reason why the Dark Queen is looking for the Green Gemstone Man, what power does he hold and what could his power mean for the companions if they find him? This novel develops the characters more (mainly Tanis and Laurana) through their interactions. People across Anaslon prepare to fight for their homes, their freedom and their lives. Will the races be able to come together and work to fight the evil within the world and save themselves?<br /><br />Hickman and Weis knock it out of the ball park with this one again. There is so much that happens within the novel that you don't want to put it down. Old favorite characters return and new ones are introduced as the companions make their way to their destination to stop the Dark Lady, a dragon highlord with a repuation. If the companions fail then the world is lost to the Dark Queen and her evil minions. Can the party put aside their own fears and insecurities to be able to save the world? Or will they crumble under the pressure?<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9262178703731097603" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7569309683235728342">I started this series because some friends told me that they loved it more than <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_' title='The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R.   <span id="freeText7569309683235728342" style="display:none">I started this series because some friends told me that they loved it more than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33.The_Lord_of_the_Rings__The_Lord_of_the_Rings___1_3_" title="The Lord of the Rings (The Lord of the Rings, #1-3) by J.R.R. Tolkien" rel="nofollow noopener">The Lord of the Rings</a>. That seemed like a fairly worth while recommendation. I was certainly surprised to discover that this not even in the same league as Tolkien. They did say that it starts out a little rough, but once you get into it the story really takes off. Well, after finishing the book I kept wondering when it was going to get better. <br /><br />After finishing it I decided that I needed to re-examined all the recommendations that these people gave me. And completely ignored them. <br /><br />Comparisons to Tolkien aside, this is a badly written book. From a grammar position all the way to the overall narrative structure and character story arcs, this book (and the trilogy) is simply awful. </span>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1645217214?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dan Call" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dan Call" href="/user/show/52049585-dan-call">Dan Call</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1645217214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14893845283210484300">Fairly predictable fantasy-adventure novel that I read about 25 years ago. I decided to go back and re-read the entire trilogy to see if there's anything more there. What really works for me in this series is the richness of the characters - almost all of them seem to sit atop a thoroughly developed backstory. Big shout-out to the authors for creating Raistlin: as fascinating a magic user as was ever written. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1181824323" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1181824323" />
    <a title="Lundos" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39592811-lundos"><img alt="Lundos" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1457806501p2/39592811.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1181824323?book_show_action=true">Jan 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lundos" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lundos" href="/user/show/39592811-lundos">Lundos</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780880381741" href="/book/show/1082246.Dragons_of_Winter_Night">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39592811-lundos?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1181824323" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16168102232233408359">It's been a long while sine I've read this and I've skipped the first one for a buddy read. <br/><br/>Still, I remembered most of the characters, and why wouldn't I? This series was the first fantasy series I read in English, so it has a strong sentimental factor. Raistlin is still - after all these years - one of my favorite characters. <br/><br/>The writing isn't pretty. At least not after just finishing Gardens of the Moon by Steven Erikson, but the story still flows very fast. I believe this was played as a D&D</span>
  <span id="freeText16168102232233408359" style="display:none">It's been a long while sine I've read this and I've skipped the first one for a buddy read. <br /><br />Still, I remembered most of the characters, and why wouldn't I? This series was the first fantasy series I read in English, so it has a strong sentimental factor. Raistlin is still - after all these years - one of my favorite characters. <br /><br />The writing isn't pretty. At least not after just finishing Gardens of the Moon by Steven Erikson, but the story still flows very fast. I believe this was played as a D&amp;D game back then, so we have a lot flashing forward to the important parts and not much (uselesss) filling. That sometimes leaves us with the issues that sometimes the authors feel they need to explain the situation and/or history from one sentence to the next. It can be annoying at times.<br /><br />If we look beyond the main struggle between good and evil - yes, this one isn't gray - this book is a lot about friendship, overcoming ordeals and sacrificing yourself for the better good. If this is sacrificing your love <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Silvara by betraying her race <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, yourself (huge spoiler) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Sturm for his friends after the Measure failed him <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, friendship <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Laurana staying at the Tower of the High Clerist for Sturm (and Tanis) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> or just the greater good <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Tas smashing the dragon orb <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> or even <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the entire dream sequence in Silvanost, where most of the dreams are about not being able to help the others <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> the themes is running through the entire book. <br /><br />The best parts - besides the above - are the development of Laurana, the shenanigans of Tas and the nobility of Sturm. <br /><br />And of course Raistlin. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Nice to see you in red. And a nice joke for them to put white on you to hide in the snow.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="16168102232233408359" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bVUBbxHz57/FqEDB3StcbUcOOMJunJkivrlUABGuB5xRIyQcypNK+XEx042MXF6DwBGEPqTop9/hcpMsLHPrNA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('vnnfEzZKhJYm/GwCnQgRTlwk2lME2oDdpcR1r3FOhTGCD/pg7Sop0JJl/07MfxOg2ztmr86uviD6D7KDTJNpmQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Every person saved increases the population of the Grotto, but is also another mouth to feed.\n\nAfter saving thousands and not finding a single familiar face, new intelligence reaches the Grotto: sending Rocky against a challenge that even the King of Apes couldn’t overcome.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"4262198358058611128\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return <span id="freeTextContainer12890283042774376333">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two para</span>
  <span id="freeText12890283042774376333" style="display:none">Fantasy novelist who, along with Tracy Hickman, was one of the original creators of the <i>Dragonlance</i> game world. I've written numerous novels and short stories set in the world of Krynn, as well as series in other, original worlds. These include: Darksword, Rose of the Prophet, Star of the Guardians, DeathGate, Dragonvarld, Sovereign Stone, Dragonships, and the Dragon Brigade. I also wrote two paranormal romance novels, Fallen Angel and Warrior Angel, with my daughter, Elizabeth Baldwin. I graduated from the University of Missouri–Columbia and now live in Wisconsin with dogs, Max, Dixie, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am currently working on the third book in the Dragon Brigade series, the Seventh Sigil. The first book is Shadow Raiders. The second book is Storm Riders, coming out from Tor in July 2013. <br /><br />My hobby is flyball racing with my dogs, Dixie, a border collie, and two crackhead Shelties, Joey the Thug and Clancy the Hooligan. <br /><br />I am the owner of the company, Margaret Weis Productions, publisher of RPGs. Our newest project is creating the RPG for the wonderful TV series, Firefly. Shiny!</span>

He asked me what they did and I demonstated and he said they were 'glasses of true seeing.' The dwarven magic-users of old made them to read books written in other languages and--" Tas stopped.<br />"And?" Tanis pursued.<br />"And--uh--magic spellbooks."
